Attending Representatives and Guests Municipal Government Representative Zhu Xusheng, Hankou General Chamber of Commerce Jia Ruifang, Bankers' Association Gan Sheng Teng, Jiangsu High Court Second Branch Dai Hongquan, Supervisor Auditor Zhou Zengkui, Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Wang Yansong, Money Trade Association Yan Junan, Fund Committee Lin Kanghou, Lottery Drawers Central Bank Li Xisheng, Bank of China Cheng Muhao, Bank of Communications Jin Wenyuan, Administrators Zhu Zuohong, Lu Shutang, He Xiaowei, Pang Zeen, Registrars Liang Yaozong, Chen Shaochao, He Junchao, Ji Juncai, Clerks Huang Qizong, Xu Zuhuang, Huang Meichuan, Receptionists Wang Gongshi, He Yaoqing, Luo Peide, Zhu Peigen.

Excluding the first to third repayments, which have been drawn and repaid on schedule, today marks the fourth repayment. This time, four bonds will be drawn, each worth 300,000 yuan, for a total of 1.2 million yuan. All winning bond tickets will be repaid starting from the 30th of this month by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications in various locations, along with the fourth period interest. Payment will be made in silver dollars, regardless of location. Supervisors are requested to verify the winning tickets and the stub book before the drawing.

The winning numbers for the Seventeenth Year Financial Short-Term Government Bond are 01, 27, 46, 80, totaling four bonds, with a total repayment of 1.2 million silver dollars. Repayment will be made by the Central Bank, Bank of China, and Bank of Communications in various locations, starting from the end of this month.

White Russians Forcibly Demolish Civilian Houses in Qingyun Lane, Chongming Road Yesterday 111

Over Thirty Homes Disturbed

Several Citizens Injured

Citizens' United Conference Resolves to Provide Assistance The houses in the Qingyun Lane area of North Sichuan Road and Chongming Road belong to the property of New Sassoon & Co. Recently, due to the issue of reconstruction and renovation, disputes have arisen between the owners and tenants for two months. Around 10:00 AM yesterday, over two hundred White Russians arrived in eight trucks and began demolishing houses in Qingyun Lane, starting from Qifa Grocery Store at No. 14 Chongming Road. Residents were shocked and alarmed by the sudden arrival of the White Russian workers, who entered their homes without warning. They gathered to resist, and conflicts broke out. Some were wrestling and fighting, while others were throwing tiles and bricks. Several people were injured. After the incident, the residents reported to the Hongkou Police Station, which immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives to suppress the violence and ordered the Russians to stop working and await a resolution. By 11:30 AM, this theatrical scene of demolition had come to a halt.

Demolition in Progress Qingyun Lane consists of nine lanes, with Chongming Road as the latitude, connecting Tian Road in the south and Wuchang Road in the north. There are many residents, with no fewer than five hundred households, including storefronts. The owner, New Sassoon & Co., recently proposed reconstruction, but the residents opposed it. The Tenants' Association has been negotiating with the company without success. The owner has given the tenants until the end of August to vacate the premises for demolition and plans to start demolishing over a hundred houses in lanes six to nine and along the street front. At around 10:00 AM yesterday, the owner ordered over two hundred White Russian workers to demolish the houses.

Conflict Erupts The Russian workers arrived in a fleet of eight trucks. Upon reaching their destination, they got out and entered the house of Qifa Grocery Store at No. 14. Initially, the residents were puzzled by the arrival of the large group of Russians. However, after learning the reason, they were greatly displeased. The employees of Qifa Grocery Store were shocked to see the Russians entering their house and tried to stop them, but they refused. As they did not speak the same language, a conflict broke out immediately. Those on the roof threw bricks and tiles, while those below punched and fought back. The area around Chongming Road was thrown into chaos, and the residents panicked.

The residents reported the situation to the Hongkou Police Station and requested assistance. The Police Chief led a team of armed Chinese and Western detectives to suppress the violence. However, by the time they arrived, several people had already been injured in the fighting.

Work Suspended When the police arrived, the Hongkou Fire Brigade also drove to the scene. However, as there was no fire, they quickly withdrew. The Police Chief first summoned five Russian foremen and ordered them to suspend work and await a resolution. The Russians then descended from the houses, and by around 11:30 AM, they had gradually left. By then, the roofs of over thirty houses had been damaged. Several people from both sides were injured in the chaos. Among the tenants, Miao She Lai, Ye Jingming, and Deng Tong were injured, with Miao's injuries being the most severe. There were also several cases of theft of silver dollars and clothing. The Tenants' Association held an emergency meeting overnight to discuss countermeasures and request assistance from various organizations.

Citizens' Meeting The Preparatory Committee of the Special District Citizens' United Conference held its ninth plenary committee meeting yesterday afternoon. Nineteen committee members, including She Yangsheng, Lu Qisheng, Jiang Xinzhao, and Wang Pingnan, attended. Chen Yiting was elected as the chairman. After completing the formalities, the secretary reported on the minutes of the previous meeting. The Special Committee on Rent Disputes reported on its work progress, which was approved separately. Next, the chairman reported that representatives of the North Sichuan Road Qingyun Lane Tenants' Association had reported to the conference that New Sassoon & Co. had hired hundreds of White Russian vagrants, armed with weapons, to demolish the roofs and tiles of the houses and had injured three tenants and caused countless losses of money and property. The case was serious and should be discussed immediately by changing the agenda. The motion was passed unanimously. First, the representatives of the Qingyun Lane tenants stood up to report on the cause of the incident. Then, the chairman submitted it for discussion. Committee members Yu Yangsheng, Lu Qisheng, Jiang Xinzhao, Yu Zhongxian, and Hu Fengxiang successively expressed their opinions and proposed concrete assistance measures: (1) Elect three representatives to petition the Shanghai Municipal Council to severely punish the White Russian assailants and their instigators and to ensure the maintenance of security in the district; (2) Elect representatives to visit the five Chinese directors of the Shanghai Municipal Council and ask them to expedite negotiations with the Shanghai Municipal Council; (3) Submit petitions to the Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to negotiate and protest based on reason; (4) Issue a declaration to promote awareness. The motions were passed separately and handed over to the committee for processing. Next, the method of organizing district branches was discussed, and it was decided that each committee member should be responsible for organizing them according to the regulations and then submitting them for record. Finally, other miscellaneous cases were discussed and the meeting adjourned.

Rickshaw Rent Hike 112

Heard Resolved Last Night

Resumption of Work Expected This Morning Around 2:00 PM yesterday, near the intersection of Route Tenant de la Tour and Avenue Joffre in the French Concession (where many rickshaws are rented out), some rickshaw owners wanted to increase the rent by one jiao per shift. The rickshaw pullers could not afford it, so they started a strike. Immediately, some rickshaw pullers deflated the tires of passing rickshaws, regardless of whether they had passengers, and ordered them to return the rickshaws, joining the strike. The information gathered is detailed below: (Reason) The license fees have not increased, but the major companies are increasing the rent again. Even if the major companies do not increase the rent, the small owners (those who subcontract the rickshaws) want to increase the rent by one jiao per shift, making it unaffordable for the rickshaw pullers, leading to the strike. (Rent) The major companies rent out the rickshaws for seven or eight jiao per shift. After being subcontracted several times, the small owners rent them out for one yuan per shift. Now, they want to increase it by another jiao, adding to the cost of straw sandals, lamp oil, fines, and other expenses, making it unbearable for the rickshaw pullers. (Order) According to the striking rickshaw pullers, the rent increase was not approved by the authorities, so the police did not interfere with the strike. However, some agitators (those who deflated the tires) were arrested by the Public Security Bureau near Tangjiawan. It was also reported that the Public Security Bureau believed that the number of striking rickshaw pullers was too large and unorganized, consisting of simple-minded and mixed-quality individuals who could easily be incited, posing a significant threat to social order. Therefore, upon learning of the strike, they immediately dispatched a large team of armed police officers to maintain order. (Aftermath) The rickshaw manager hired by a small owner in Dakang Lane on Route Tenant de la Tour, who usually bullies the rickshaw pullers, continued to do so during the strike. This angered the striking rickshaw pullers. Four or five women from the same lane, feeling indignant, led the way and beat him severely in retaliation for his usual bullying. (Arrests and Releases) When the commotion occurred, the police were alerted and immediately dispatched detectives to stop it. Twenty-two people were arrested on the spot and taken to the police station. After a detailed inquiry, the police determined that they were all rickshaw pullers and feared that unscrupulous individuals were inciting them. After giving them a lecture, they were immediately released. (Resolution) It was reported that the price increase was notified by the rickshaw owners to the small owners on the first of this month, with implementation scheduled for the seventh. However, some parties voluntarily compromised and reduced the increase to five fen. As the rickshaw owners are not a unified organization, the implementation varied, leading to a sudden small disturbance yesterday. As of last night, the issue has been completely resolved, with a uniform reduction to five fen. If there are no other changes, business will resume as usual today.

Sino-Japanese Telecommunications Negotiations Japanese Committee Arrives in Shanghai Today 113

Meeting in Nanjing in Mid-Month

Shanghai-Nagasaki Line to be Discussed First China and Japan have officially appointed negotiators for the Sino-Japanese telecommunications negotiations. The Chinese committee members are Hu Shize, Director of the Asian Department of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and Zhuang Zhihuan, Director of the Telecommunications Department of the Ministry of Communications. The Japanese expert committee members are Charge d'Affaires ad interim Shigemitsu Mamoru and Yoshino Keizo, Director of the Savings Bureau of the Japanese Ministry of Communications. The meeting location has been decided as Nanjing, with the date around mid-month. The Japanese committee member Yoshino, along with the secretary of the Ministry of Communications, Iino Takeo, the secretary of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Omori Kenji, and Maji Masazaburo, arrived in Shanghai from Japan on the Hikawamaru. They are expected to arrive at the Waibaidu Bridge Wharf at 1:00 PM today. After meeting with Shigemitsu, they will proceed to Nanjing to begin negotiations. The Shanghai-Nagasaki line will be discussed first, followed by the Fuzhou-Taiwan line, the Qingdao-Sasebo line, and the Dalian-Zhifu line.

San De Tang and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Correspondences 114

Agreed to Renew Lease or Purchase Wharf

But Wording Still Evasive

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Declares Extension for Arbitration In the Jinliyuan Wharf case of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, after both parties appointed arbitrators, the French arbitrator, Yamina, acted entirely as an arbitrator for the annulment of the contract, and everything was restrained by the French Court, violating the provisions of the arbitration agreement. Fortunately, the French Consul-General, Kammerer, sincerely mediated, preventing a complete breakdown. Now, the representative of San De Tang has sent a letter to the lawyer of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Tietbeck, agreeing to renew the lease or purchase the wharf. However, it was verbally stated that the French Bishop had left Paris for the countryside, and the price had not yet been estimated, and negotiations had not begun. The General Manager of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Cai, has notified the French Court and San De Tang of the statement. The various news items are detailed below:

French Consul-General's Sincere Expression The French Consul-General telegraphed Lawyer Gao Shuo yesterday morning to discuss the San De Tang case and promised to wait for a reply from Paris and persuade the priest to settle peacefully as soon as possible. The communication was very satisfactory.

San De Tang's Letter to China Merchants Steam Navigation Company "Letter from Lawyer Barreau, Representative of San De Tang, to Lawyer Tietbeck, Representative of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company," (Translation) Sir, in the case of the San De Tang and China Merchants Steam Navigation Company lease dispute, on the 19th of this month, the French Concession Mixed Court ruled to give China Merchants Steam Navigation Company a final deadline of September 15th of this year to select an arbitrator as stipulated in the first instance judgment of January 7th of this year and the appellate judgment of May 23rd. On the same day, our client received a letter from the General Manager of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company stating that they had selected Lawyer Gao Shuo as their full representative. However, the letter stated that the French Consul had taken steps to prevent the execution of the judgment, which is quite alarming. Lawyer Gao Shuo subsequently visited Yamina, the arbitrator of San De Tang, but according to Lawyer Gao, the scope of arbitration was not limited to that stipulated in the two judgments and insisted on re-arbitrating the entire case. Yamina stated that this was not possible and informed him that his arbitration report had already been submitted to the court. Lawyer Gao could either follow his report or submit his own opinion. If they disagreed, the two arbitrators would jointly appoint a third arbitrator, or the court would appoint Yamina to review his report. However, today's newspapers reported that the above situation, based on a semi-official telegram from Nanjing, was completely inconsistent with the facts and was a threatening propaganda. Although the French Consul had mediated during the dispute to persuade the two parties to continue amicable negotiations, if the negotiations broke down, the judgment of the French Court would still be executed. The French Consul has no intention of interfering with justice and has no such power. As a result of the French Consul's mediation, there are two options: (1) On the 26th of this month, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company sent a letter to the French Consul stating that they had obtained the consent of the Ningpo Commercial & Savings Bank to guarantee the payment of future rent and requested the French Consul to instruct San De Tang to begin arbitration as soon as possible; (2) San De Tang telegraphed its headquarters in Paris to seek agreement to sell the X-shaped base and wharf at No. 69 to China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. This method is most appropriate and will permanently avoid future disputes. San De Tang hereby explains its position in four points: (1) The cancellation of the lease is a confirmed fact. If the two parties cannot reach an agreement within a very short period of time, the judgment should be executed according to the court's instructions. The arbitrator's task is only to verify the details of the execution and cannot exceed the scope set by the court order to negotiate new contracts or other methods. However, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company can still fully authorize its lawyer or other representatives to directly negotiate with the San De Tang priest to reach an agreement, negotiate a new contract, or purchase the wharf to permanently resolve the current dispute and avoid future disputes; (2) Before the agreement is reached, the arbitration must still proceed as usual and must be completed by September 15th at the latest. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's arbitrator, Lawyer Gao, should submit the arbitration report as soon as possible so that a third arbitrator can be selected to resolve any disagreements between the two arbitrators; (3) China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has not paid our client the rent for this term. All rent collected from this year onwards and the rent payable after the judgment before China Merchants Steam Navigation Company vacates are due. However, China Merchants Steam Navigation Company cannot use this as an excuse to hope to restore the lease that has already been cancelled. This should be clearly stated; (4) The bank guarantee provided by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company should be issued by the guarantor, specifying the guarantor's obligations. Although China Merchants Steam Navigation Company has resorted to despicable methods, there is still a possibility of reconciliation between the two parties. Please inform your client to engage in substantive negotiations and not to use newspaper propaganda as a tool, which may lead to reconciliation. Sincerely, Lawyer Tietbeck, Barreau, August 1930.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Letter to San De Tang "Letter from General Manager Cai Peiji of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company directly to the French Court's San De Tang, refuting the letter from Lawyer Barreau's representative," issued yesterday, stated that the delay was the responsibility of San De Tang. According to the report of Lawyer Gao Shuo, the arbitrator of the company, (1) Yamina, the arbitrator of the other party, expressed his views and sent a letter to Lawyer Gao, which took four days; (2) Bishop Xia Lou telegraphed the headquarters in Paris to inquire about the sale price, but has not yet received a reply. If all the issues are discussed individually, it will take several months to resolve them. China Merchants Steam Navigation Company is willing to sincerely accept the French Consul-General's kind mediation and resolve everything as soon as possible. September 15th is the deadline set by the court, and the two parties must request a postponement. Finally, it was said that San De Tang is a charitable organization of the church, and the two parties, as landlord and tenant, have a considerable amount of affection for each other. It is hoped that they will be open and honest with each other and resolve the matter as soon as possible to maintain friendship and live up to the French Consul-General's efforts to mediate.

China Merchants Steam Navigation Company to be Managed by Government under Commercial Operation

Date of Mr. Li's Assumption According to Mr. Cai, he has met with General Manager Li many times. High Court Yesterday Heard童三毛's Appeal Case 116

Conspired Suicide, Rescued and Saved

According to the Law, He Should Be Exempted from Punishment

童's Lawyer Made This Request

The Court Ordered the Verdict to Be Announced on the 15th. The case of 童三毛 from Ningbo, who coerced the dancing girl 黃白英 to take poison, but she was rescued and survived, once caused a sensation. 童 was prosecuted by the police for attempted instigation of murder in the Special District Local Court and sentenced to two years of imprisonment. Dissatisfied, he appealed to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court, which scheduled the trial for September 10, as previously reported. Yesterday afternoon, the appointed date arrived, and the police escorted 童 to the First Criminal Court of the High Court Branch. 童 wore a sticky colored Western suit, a pale blue shirt, and a straw hat. Although he had been detained for over two months, he did not appear to be in a state of decline. After the trial began, 童 held his hat in his hand. However, 黃白英 had gone to Hong Kong and was therefore unable to appear in court. Judge 宋沅, assessors 高君湘 and 葉在疇, as well as the prosecutor and clerk, took their seats. First, three other cases involving the promotion of doctrines incompatible with the Three Principles of the People were judged. Then, the 童 case was addressed. Judge 宋 asked 童 his age, place of origin, address, and profession. He then ordered him to give a detailed account of the case's process and the grounds for his appeal. 童 then recounted everything from his acquaintance with 黃白英 to the events after she took poison, her admission to 寳隆 Hospital for treatment, and the circumstances under which the police dispatched detectives to investigate the hospital and arrest him. His statements were entirely consistent with his testimony in the first instance trial, without any discrepancies, so there was no need to elaborate. Next, the witnesses were called, including 方衡年, who had ridden with 童三毛 and 黃白英 in a car on the night of June 28 from outside the Paris Dance Hall to the western suburbs of Shanghai, as well as the driver and the tea server from Room 101 of the Cangzhou Hotel. They were interrogated in turn. After each person gave a detailed account of what they knew, Judge 宋 ordered the start of the debate. 童's defense lawyer stated that the most important witness in the case, 黃白英, was absent. He asked whether it would be possible to summon her to court for interrogation before proceeding with the debate. The judge replied that the police were handling the matter concerning 黃白英, so it was not necessary for her to be present in person. The lawyer then defended his client, 童三毛. He first analyzed the facts, stating that 童's actions that night were insufficient to prove any intention to instigate suicide. He also attacked 黃白英's testimony during the first trial. Next, he discussed the law, saying that it did not constitute the crime of instigating suicide but rather a form of conspired suicide, rescued and saved, for which, according to the law, he should be exempted from punishment or granted a suspended sentence. Finally, he stated that the reason 黃白英 accused 童 was that she had been misled by her new lover, surnamed Zhang. 黃 initially wanted to die with 童, but after being rescued, she testified in court that 童 had coerced her to take poison, which was the result of her ingratiating herself with Zhang. As for 童's statement today that the pills were poured onto the table at the time and, in the blink of an eye, not only were all the pills gone, but even the bottle containing the pills had disappeared, 黃 actually did not swallow them, etc. If this were indeed the case, then it would be similar to the actions of a prostitute treating a patron in the past. In the past, prostitutes would always cut their hair to show their love when their patrons were about to leave. Dancing girls are only one step away from prostitutes, so it is difficult to guarantee that she did not agree to take poison on one hand while taking the opportunity to discard the pills on the other. Next, police lawyer 厲志山 argued, saying that the appellant believed that 黃白英 was not present today and there was no one to confront, but the transcripts of the first trial were all available and could be used to evade responsibility. The elements of the crime of instigating suicide are that another person has suicidal intent and only makes the decision after being instigated. The appellant's instigation of suicide involved all means of enticement, intimidation, deception, and assistance. 黃's motive for suicide stemmed from wanting to marry someone surnamed Zhang, but the appellant threatened her, saying that there would be a danger to the lives of two or more people. 黃 was afraid that there would be an accident after the marriage. Although Zhang wanted to marry her, 黃 was unwilling to be a concubine because he already had a wife. She was in a dilemma and had the idea of suicide. 童 then bought the pills for her and expressed his desire to die together. After 黃 took the pills, he took care of himself alone. Isn't this enticement, intimidation, deception, and assistance? If 童 had a sincere intention to commit suicide together, even if the pills had been taken completely, he could have either jumped into the sea or shot himself. 黃白英 is not present today, and the details cannot be fully known, but it is not difficult to imagine from the fact that 童's family made a special trip to the 黃 family during the first trial. Therefore, the appellant cannot overturn all the testimony in this case. The sentence of two years' imprisonment in the first trial was already extremely lenient. At the time, the police thought that 童 was young and that two years of imprisonment might reform him. He requested that the original verdict be upheld and rejected his request for a suspended sentence, let alone an exemption from punishment. 童's lawyer then offered another rebuttal before the conclusion was announced. The court ordered that the verdict be announced at 2:00 PM on the 15th of this month. 童三毛 was still taken back to the police station for detention by the police. The time was exactly 5:30.

Kidnapping Case in 陳家行 and 邢家堰, Pudong 119

The area of 邢家堰 in Tangkou South River, Chenxing Township, Pudong, has always been peaceful. The residents are mostly engaged in farming and are simple and have ancient customs. Unexpectedly, a kidnapping case occurred the day before yesterday. Initially, there was a person named 邢吟泉 in the area who made a living by farming and had a small ancestral estate. He had a grown son. That night, he was at home. A month ago, he had received several anonymous letters demanding a large sum of money, with the general meaning, "If you don't reply, it shows that you have no sincerity in negotiating. If that is the case, then we will take action. We ask you to pay special attention," etc. He ignored them all, which angered the bandits. It had not been a day or two. The house next to 吟泉 was occupied by his nephew. That night at 11:00 PM, six bandits knocked on the door of 邢's nephew's house. Amidst the commotion, they mistakenly bound and kidnapped 邢尧生 (25 years old), 吟泉's nephew, and 尧生's younger brother. At the time, 吟泉 heard the noise and knew it was bandits. He did not dare to go out to investigate, so he took his son to the roof to avoid them and fortunately escaped unharmed. Later, he saw the bandits holding weapons and heading southwest along the official road leading directly to Dujiahang Town in the moonlight. He waited to report to the Chenxing Town Public Security Bureau and the Security Corps and requested them to pursue the bandits, but they had already disappeared without a trace. According to 吟泉, the bandits seemed to be former water patrolmen who spoke fluent Northern dialect and wore dark gray clothes.

Extortion Leads to Murder 120

吳德忠, a native of Yancheng, 28 years old, made a living pulling rickshaws and selling soy milk. He currently lived with his aunt, 吳唐氏 (44 years old), at 9 Fuxing Lane, Xinqiao Road, Nanshi. 吳's wife, 高氏, was the same age as 吳. The couple had a close relationship and had two sons. The eldest, 大祥子, was 7 years old, and the younger, 小祥子, was only 3 years old. The hall at number 9 was rented by 唐茂相, a tutor, who ran a private school with more than 30 students, mostly children of laborers. The tuition he received was barely enough to make ends meet. 吳 had a cousin named 德隆 who was also a rickshaw puller. He lived in the French Concession at the home of his uncle, 吳祥生, in 公記 Lane. Yesterday afternoon around 5:00 PM, 德隆 suddenly gathered a group of hooligans and went directly to 9 Fuxing Lane. He called 唐茂相 to a nearby teahouse to talk. 唐 had just dismissed school, so he went with them to the teahouse. Unexpectedly, 德隆 told 唐 that 唐 was having an affair with 德忠's wife. He was aggressive and intended to extort money. 唐 sternly refused. 德隆 became angry and went to Fuxing Lane, shouting that 唐 and 高氏 were sleeping together outside. At the time, 德忠 had just finished work and returned home. He suddenly heard these words. He knew that his wife was virtuous and 唐 was a scholar. He reasoned that 德隆 was deliberately trying to extort money. However, he was afraid of 德隆's violence and the hooligans he had gathered, so he did not dare to confront him. He went upstairs in shame and, out of anger and frustration, committed suicide by hanging himself in the west corner of the building. By the time people noticed, he had been dead for a long time. His aunt, 唐氏, reported the situation to the Liyuan Road Substation of the Second District General Office. Officer Wang heard the news and immediately sent Patrol Chief Shen to investigate. When they went to pursue 德隆, he had already heard the news and fled. At the time, 唐氏 suspected that 德隆's aunt, 吳張氏 (32 years old), had instigated and incited him, so she took her to the Second District General Office as well. The office ordered the local bailiff to report the matter for inspection and prepared a document to transfer the case to the Judicial Section for investigation.

Husband Abandons Wife Because of One Person's Words 121

Wife Attempts Suicide in Anger. A young woman from Beiping named 啹姚氏, 25 years old, and her husband, 德興, had previously served as a county magistrate in the northern provinces and had accumulated some savings. Later, he resigned and came to Shanghai, renting a house at 105 Hexing Lane, Baoxing Road, Zhabei, for two years. Due to the dangerous symptoms, the hospital transferred her to Guangren Hospital for treatment.

Passenger on Songhu Train Falls and is Crushed to Death 124

The 89th train on the Songhu Railway, traveling upstream, departed from Zhanghuabang Station at 1:29 PM yesterday. As it was traveling to Liyangqitai, a middle-aged man suddenly jumped from a third-class car and fell onto the tracks. He was immediately crushed by the train wheels, and his head and arms were broken. He died instantly. The scene was bloody and gruesome. After the accident, the train stopped. The conductor and ticket collector got off the train and, together with the station master, removed the body. They found that the deceased was about thirty years old, wearing a straw hat, with a monk's haircut, a white undershirt, white and blue striped Western trousers, black socks, and rubber galoshes. Local bailiff 秦寳林 took the train to report to the local court for inspection. The conductor reported to the Road Bureau's Traffic Department for handling.

Human Trafficking Case Cracked on the Jinan Ship 127

Five people, including men, women, and children, were arrested. The Taikoo Company's Hong Kong-bound Jinan steamship was about to set sail and leave the port at 11:00 AM yesterday. Investigators Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang from the Women and Children Relief Association boarded the ship to investigate. They saw an elderly man wearing a Western suit and an old woman in the steerage cabin, bringing a young girl and two children, a boy and a girl. They looked like human traffickers, so they questioned them. Unexpectedly, their words were inconsistent, and the situation was extremely suspicious. They were immediately detained and the Water Patrol Police were notified by telephone. Officer Huang Songsheng was immediately dispatched to take the five people, big and small, to the police station for separate interrogation. According to the man, he was named Yang Shoulai, 53 years old, from Zhongshan County, Guangdong Province. He used to be a supervisor at the Telephone Company and had retired. His wife had also passed away. He was now living with a widow named Wang (referring to the old woman) at 572 Qiujiang Road, Zhabei. He had three brothers in Hong Kong who had no children. Therefore, he spent money to buy the two children, a boy and a girl, to take to Hong Kong and give to his brothers as children. The young girl, Yang A'mei, was also bought as a daughter by him when she was eight years old. Today, they sent us to board the ship but did not go to Hong Kong, etc. According to the old woman, her surname was Wang, 48 years old, from Beiping. Her husband had died early, leaving behind two sons and a daughter. The eldest son, A'tong, 18 years old, was learning to be a switchboard operator at the telephone bureau. The second son, A'song (the boy who was caught), was 7 years old, and the daughter, A'nan (the girl who was caught), was 10 years old. They were all her children, etc. According to the young girl, her name was Yang A'mei, 16 years old, from Guangdong. She answered that she did not know what was asked. According to the boy, his name was A'song, 7 years old, born in the Year of the Rat, from Tianjin. His parents both lived in the French Concession, and he had forgotten the address. He had four brothers at home and was the third. He had been to the woman's (referring to Wang's) house two weeks ago. The woman was not his mother. Today, he did not know where she was taking him. According to the girl, her name was A'nan, 10 years old, from Ningbo. She had heard her mother (referring to Wang) talk about how she was sent to live with someone else as a baby and was only brought back when she was four years old. She did not know if she was born to Wang, etc. The police chief investigated the case and found that the statements of the five people were very different. The adults and children spoke Cantonese, Northern dialect, and Ningbo dialect. What was even stranger was that the boy denied that Wang was his mother, even though Wang claimed that the two children were her own. The girl also had doubts about Wang and did not directly recognize her as her mother. It was obvious that they were not telling the truth. At 2:00 PM, he ordered Detective Wu Rongsheng to take the five people, big and small, to the local court for interrogation.

Zhang Zhu's Lawsuit for Divorce 129

Yesterday, the debate did not start.

The standard for identifying syphilis is that the young woman Zhang Zhu's is only seventeen years old, is a native of Cixi, Ningbo. Last year, on November 26 of the lunar calendar, with Xu Juxing, Lou Shunxing, and others as matchmakers, she married Zhang Yuefang. Unexpectedly, they soon quarreled. Now, she has hired lawyer Jiang Yiping to file a divorce lawsuit with the local court, asking for 4,000 yuan in compensation and the return of 1,094 yuan in dowry and clothing. The total request is 5,094 yuan. The reason is that the defendant has syphilis, which the plaintiff was infected with, and was abused and beaten, resulting in injuries, with blood-stained clothing as evidence. She requested permission to divorce. The defendant, Zhang Yuefang, also hired lawyer Sha Xunyi to respond and filed a counterclaim requesting cohabitation. His statement was roughly as follows: Since the plaintiff's return to her mother's home, the relationship between the two parties has been very close. Unfortunately, the plaintiff's mother is very violent. In May of this year, the counterclaimant's father was critically ill. The plaintiff's mother repeatedly instructed her daughter to make noise and divide the property. The counterclaimant's father could not bear the disturbance, so he wrote a will. On June 2, the counterclaimant's father died. At this point, the plaintiff repeatedly requested to manage and divide the rights to the entire property she obtained. The counterclaimant did not agree because of the property rights, and a quarrel broke out. Her mother helped from the sidelines. On June 22, the plaintiff returned to her mother's home. On the 28th, the counterclaimant personally went to pick her up. Unexpectedly, after returning for one night, she asked the counterclaimant for five yuan the next day, ostensibly to buy shoes. She left and never returned. Unexpectedly, the plaintiff secretly took a bank savings book (with 200 yuan) and jewelry. She requested that the claim be rejected and ordered to cohabit, etc. The reasons are divided into two points: (A) The evidence of syphilis is easily transmitted. However, whether the transmission is from B to A or from A to B, even a famous doctor may not be able to determine. The counterclaimant is now in good health and shows no signs of syphilis. The plaintiff's request for divorce based on this uncertain fact has no legal basis. This is the first illegal request to reject the plaintiff's claim. (B) The claim of being beaten and injured is even more fabricated. There are conditions for injury to constitute divorce, which cannot be asserted with empty words. The plaintiff's complaint did not state where the injury was, what part of the body was harmed, or even the number of times, date, or year of the beating. She only used the words "blood-stained clothing as evidence" as confirmation of the request for divorce. Whether this kind of blood-stained clothing is fake or real is unknown, but it lacks the necessary elements for legal research and cannot be considered true. This is the second illegal request to reject the plaintiff's claim, etc. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge 童繩履 specially opened the Fourth Court for trial. Both parties arrived with their lawyers. First, the plaintiff Zhang Zhu's stated that she was 17 years old, from Ningbo, and lived at her uncle's house in Wuxing Lane, Beller Road. The interrogating official said, "You are not old enough." The plaintiff replied, "My mother is in the audience." The official ordered the plaintiff's mother, Zhu Lin's, to come forward and state that she was 38 years old this year. The official asked, "Do you know that your daughter is filing a lawsuit?" She replied, "I know." The official ordered Lin's to step down and asked Zhang Zhu's what kind of request she had. She replied, "I request a divorce and the return of my dowry, clothing, and compensation, etc." He asked, "What is the reason?" She replied, "He beats me, even causing me to bleed." He asked, "Is it the blood on the clothes?" She replied, "Yes." (She was wearing a white short shirt stained with blood, and there was also a tear of about an inch at the neckline). He asked, "When did you get married?" She replied, "We got married on November 26 of last year. I have headaches and stomachaches because I have been beaten many times." He asked, "When did he beat you?" She replied, "He beat me on June 7 and 18 of this year. I went to Guangci Hospital for treatment." He asked, "Do you have the savings book with 200 yuan?" She replied, "Yes, it is mine."

Page 12

The official ordered the defendant Zhang Yuefang to come forward and state that he was 25 years old, from Dinghai, lived at 1 Yongxing Lane, Zongyu Lane, Zhabei, and currently worked on a ship. He asked, "Did you hit her?" He replied, "No." He asked, "Do you have syphilis?" He replied, "No." The interrogating official attempted mediation in court, but the plaintiff insisted on divorce, so the mediation failed. The interrogating official then said to the lawyers of both parties, "We will not start the debate today. We will wait for both parties to be tested for syphilis and then set a date for a continued hearing." After the order was issued, the court adjourned.

Trade Association News 131

Export Hat Industry The Export Hat Industry Association, regarding the Cao Mao Donation Bureau established by Bao merchants in Zhejiang Province, illegally collected donations on exported Cao Mao. After learning of this, the association convened a meeting the other day. Chairman Yang Wenlin delivered a speech, roughly stating that in the seventeenth year of the Republic of China, the National Government, in order to develop national trade and protect the livelihoods of ordinary people, approved the request of the association. The Ministry of Finance issued a notice to all customs bureaus stating that all Cao Mao exports would be exempt from taxes and duties. This has been implemented for a long time. Recently, Cao Mao merchants in Zhejiang Province have insisted that exported Cao Mao be sold domestically, arbitrarily levying harsh taxes, deliberately creating difficulties, not only harming industry and commerce, but also disregarding the Ministry's orders. Regarding how to deal with this matter, most of the members decided to send Ma Zhongda, Wang Bingyan, Sun Deyu, and Chuan Jiliang as representatives to conduct on-site investigations in Yuyao, the production area. According to the investigation report yesterday, the situation was indeed true. The four representatives then went to Hangzhou to present the matter to the Zhejiang Finance Department. Chief Jiang received them. After the representatives reported the actual situation, they requested that the various bureaus be notified immediately to prevent such acts of harming merchants and disturbing the people from happening again. After hearing this, Chief Jiang also agreed and promised to issue a notice. He also said that if the bureau illegally collects taxes, the representatives can file a complaint with the court.

Silk and Satin Industry The Silk and Satin Industry Association held its second executive committee meeting yesterday. Chairman Lu Zhengbing. The agenda was as follows: (1) The Municipal Chamber of Commerce forwarded the Social Bureau's instructions, stating that in the future, if merchants encounter liquidation matters, they should handle them in accordance with the Accountants Act, and not follow the customs and adopt incomplete liquidation procedures. It was resolved that all members be notified accordingly. (2) Regarding the failure to reach a consensus on increasing cargo plates, please reiterate the previous proposal and implement it earnestly. It was resolved to notify all members that from September 1st, an additional 1.5 fen of tin should be added, and no discrepancies should be allowed. (3) The Ministry of Industry and Commerce announced the revised Article 10 of the Implementing Rules of the Industry and Commerce Association Law regarding the number of member representatives, which is inconsistent with Article 12 of the Association's Articles of Association. Regarding the request to amend the Ministry's order, it was resolved that Article 12 of the Association's Articles of Association, which states that each company can elect one representative, be changed to "can elect one to two representatives." The last sentence of the same article, "but not more than two," be changed to "but not more than three." This will be submitted for ratification at the members' general meeting. (4) The end of September in the Gregorian calendar is the time for autumn festival account settlements. All debts between the Association's members and various customer groups must be settled on schedule. It was resolved to distribute a notice and strictly comply.

Tobacco Exchange Industry The Tobacco Exchange Industry Association held its sixth executive committee meeting yesterday. First, the chairman reported on the progress of various association affairs. Then, the following proposals were discussed: (1) Xiang Mao Soap, the manager of China Soap Company, previously offered prize draws to promote sales to members of the Association, which encouraged many to actively sell on consignment. However, the company's current prize draw methods are unfair, and members are deeply suspicious. Regarding how to discuss and deal with this matter, it was resolved to convene a general meeting of all consigning members at 1:00 PM on the 11th of this month, and to invite representatives from relevant companies to attend and discuss appropriate measures together. (2) The recent price drop of Fairy Brand cigarettes has caused significant losses to tobacco shops in the north and south that purchased the goods previously. Regarding how to calculate this, it was resolved to send a letter to the company to inquire about the details. (3) The Candle Industry Association sent a letter requesting that the Association inform its members engaged in the candle industry to voluntarily abolish the practice of giving gifts with purchases in order to protect each other's costs. It was resolved to reply to the Association, expressing a strong willingness to cooperate, but requiring them to be responsible for ensuring that no candle industry member engages in this practice again. Finally, other important matters were discussed and the meeting adjourned.

Special Article

Industrial Rationalization (Continued) by Cheng Zhenjun 133

Extreme prosperity inevitably leads to decline, which is also the result of fierce competition. Therefore, the government should adopt a laissez-faire policy, allowing people to develop freely and adjust freely, only protecting the property they have acquired through competition, and industries will inevitably prosper. This principle has not changed for more than a hundred years. Although the government has sometimes imposed restrictions for the benefit of the people, and the people have mutually exempted themselves from competition, and have jointly set prices and complied with them, or have merged into large companies, it is ultimately felt that the material life of the world is extremely complex and that it is beyond human power to organize and control it. Today, the unpredictable fall of prices, the overproduction, the large number of unemployed, the imperfect organization of enterprise institutions, and the annual loss of money are all due to the crudeness of economic principles and the failure to conduct in-depth research, the laissez-faire economic policy and the failure to manage with concerted efforts. The International Economic Conference, aware of these malpractices, followed the successful experience of Germany and proposed the suggestion of industrial rationalization to the world. The chorus of welcome from various countries has long been deafening. Some have established special agencies to implement it, while others have set up similar agencies to carry out the work in different ways. The Japanese are also chanting the mantra, and the words "industrial rationalization" (the Japanese word for industry is the same as our word for industry) are often seen on the lecture stage and in magazines and newspapers. In our country, however, it is still silent. Some may say that our country has been plagued by years of war, and people have been displaced, so how can we have the leisure to follow the new suggestions of the League of Nations? However, the war will eventually end, and the front line will not extend to the whole country. As long as we still have a breath, and have a little room to maneuver, we should widely disseminate this new economic thought and new economic plan, which is related to everyone and everything. Is not our central government still striving for construction during the difficult and arduous period of suppressing rebellion? Are not all provinces of our country, in the midst of disasters and calamities, still united from top to bottom, persevering and resolutely carrying out construction in different ways? At this time of concerted construction, there should naturally be the most excellent economic thought and the most suitable economic plan to lead the way, so as not to waste funds and go astray, and the poverty of the whole country can be alleviated. Industrial rationalization is the most excellent and most suitable economic thought and economic plan for our country. Our country has always lacked research, while rationalization emphasizes research; our country has always been unscientific, while rationalization emphasizes science; our country has always been indifferent to the success or failure of the people's industries, the high or low of prices, while rationalization emphasizes management; our country consumes a great deal in all aspects, while rationalization emphasizes eliminating consumption; our country has recently experienced many labor-capital disputes, while rationalization emphasizes labor-capital cooperation. The rest can be inferred by analogy, and there is no need to elaborate. In short, rationalization is indeed a good medicine for saving our country. We should welcome it with 120,000% sincerity. When we welcome it, we should also have a belief, that is, to examine things with scientific methods. Only in this way can we be said to accept rationalization, because rationalization must first be reformed in thought. Mr. F.W. Taylor of the United States, the inventor of scientific management, when asked about the meaning of scientific management, often replied, "This is a revolution in thought." His meaning is that scientific management cannot be merely prescribed by a plan, because it contains a new attitude of mind. Rationalization is also the same. The mind must be changed first, and then the plan can be discussed. Gentlemen, have your minds accepted rationalization? If it has been accepted, I will continue to talk about its plan. If it has not yet been accepted, please study the above carefully, and only look at the following when you are willing to accept it. The scope of rationalization is very broad, almost all-encompassing. How can I talk about its plan in a short article? However, if I omit it and do not talk about it, it seems that people will still not understand what rationalization is doing and how to implement it. I dare to summarize and briefly describe the outline, and extend it, hoping that in the future, according to history and the order of evolution, the foundation of all economic life is of course in agriculture, and there are many things that should be done for agricultural rationalization, such as weather forecasting, soil analysis, testing of various fertilizers, testing of various seeds, selection or modification of farm tools, whether or not machinery is suitable for use, how to build water conservancy projects, in order to permanently avoid water and drought disasters, how to eliminate insect pests, how to plan agricultural economics, how to manage farms, and how to organize agricultural extension. All of these should be studied and tested with scientific methods to obtain rational results and implement them. It is absolutely impossible to rely solely on personal experience or the traditional methods passed down from ancient times, and to stick to them without breaking them. It is especially impossible to rely solely on intuition and act arbitrarily. Animal husbandry and fisheries should also be managed using the latest methods. All methods of grading, selling, storing, and packaging food, and food preservation, must be specially researched by experts, and the most appropriate methods must be selected and promoted. The unnecessary consumption saved in the process cannot be measured by quantity. Furthermore, regarding the manufacture of factories, there are many types of factories, and they cannot be described separately. Here, I will specifically focus on their common matters and briefly list the uses of rationalization as follows. All factories should employ technical experts to be responsible for design and other work. The manufacturing methods and products should be researched and improved from time to time. If the machinery is defective or the tools are unfavorable, they should also be replaced with the superior ones obtained from the tests. The cost must be gradually reduced, and the output must be gradually improved or increased. Sometimes, supervisors or workers can express very effective opinions, and the factory should naturally find ways to encourage them. In terms of labor, either replace it with machinery, or change the method of exertion, or remove inconvenient places, or increase safety measures. All of these are sufficient to reduce labor and save expenses. In modern times, major factories use continuous processing and conveyor systems, which can increase efficiency several times. The finished products are strictly inspected to ensure that they meet the specified standards, which can also increase credibility and facilitate sales. Moreover, scientific inventions, obtained from trials and research, often give manufacturing a new look and shock the world, such as the paper temperature coking of coal and the multi-faceted refining of diesel, are examples. Every factory has my consumption, and eliminating consumption is an important goal of rationalization, and should be paid attention to and researched everywhere, in everything, and at all times, so that consumption can be eradicated. Furthermore, in terms of management, scientific management in the United States has long become a specialized discipline in universities, and its use in factories and stores has achieved great results. Scientific management is a part of rationalization, such as organization, cost planning, daily affairs, office methods, statistics, employment of employees, purchase of raw materials, labor-capital relations, markets, transportation, sales, advertising, and financial forecasting, all of which must be studied item by item using scientific methods, and then efficiency can be increased. Speaking of production and distribution, there are many more rational laws that can be adopted, because distribution consumes the most, and many of the middlemen can be eliminated. In recent times, mass production has meant that producers have often researched market issues themselves, and do not rely on wholesalers. Moreover, customers often want to deliver goods by a certain date and purchase directly, and there cannot be too many twists and turns. From this, issues of local purchasing power, advertising issues, trademarks and packaging issues, and even the issue of manufacturing and retailing together, are all studied in detail using scientific methods to find rational solutions and implement them. At present, many distribution businesses are still in the hands of retailers, and retailers cannot achieve the benefits enjoyed by large enterprises. In fact, they can also be managed by cooperative methods. Recently, department stores have developed greatly because management can be centralized and buyers are very convenient. There is also a type of chain store specializing in the same business, which can make large-scale purchases and compare business conditions and goods in various places. Now there are even more advanced chain department stores appearing, which combine the benefits of chain stores and department stores into one. In this distribution work, issues such as the sale, display, storage, packaging, and transportation of goods to customers can all be studied using scientific methods. From the salesperson at the counter to the general manager, the manual procedures in between can often save a lot and achieve huge economic benefits. Wholesalers or retailers can also learn about the trends of customer needs to determine changes in styles, and can explore their psychology to determine the number of buyers of a certain type of goods. These are all matters that should be paid attention to in distribution. Furthermore, in terms of consumers, there is value in researching food, clothing, and housing. Nutritious foods are not necessarily expensive, and dazzling fabrics cannot resist the cold. If you put a little thought into home furnishings, you can often increase beauty and convenience without spending anything or spending very little. As for the various unnecessary displays of extravagance in weddings, funerals, and celebrations, and the various unnecessary social interactions of giving gifts and inviting guests, all of these should be drastically reduced to a minimum. The habits and customs passed down through the ages should all be re-examined, retaining what is rational and removing what is irrational, without any compromise. This is called rationalization. All the money saved by eliminating consumption should be saved in banks or invested in real industries to make finance circulate and industries develop, and to save China from poverty. These are all the responsibilities of the people, and are also matters that should be included in rationalization. The above are the directions in which rationalization is carried out in terms of production, manufacturing, distribution, and consumption. Now, in terms of industry and commerce, from small organizations to large organizations, some of the important methods that various countries have implemented in rationalization and received great results are briefly described below. For very small enterprises, such as those that employ only two to twelve employees, there are also many work methods and equipment that need to be studied in detail. Employers cannot be engineers, business experts, economists, and psychologists at the same time, but they can often contact these academies or purchase their publications so that they can learn about and apply various knowledge. They can also discuss and study with their peers and strive for cooperation. They must not continue to hold on to the idea of secrecy, thinking that their peers will be jealous and compete with each other. It must be known that the main purpose of rationalization is to eliminate competition. Many of our country's businesses and industries have been ruined by competition, often lowering prices to the point where the selling price is lower than the cost, and they have to resort to many tricks to deceive customers. Although there are public agreements among the same trade, they are regarded as worthless. If this is not changed for a long time, they will all perish together. Therefore, changing competition into cooperation is the first essential. Medium-sized production and distribution companies face even more organizational problems that urgently need scientific research and control to achieve good results. Otherwise, responsibilities will be unclear, blame will be shifted, consumption will be high, and disputes will arise repeatedly. This must be taken seriously. Our country's business companies have absolutely no appropriate organization. All businesses rely on the planning of one or two people, which is the same as the Western so-called "rule of thumb." However, the rule of thumb is unscientific and absolutely cannot coexist with scientific management. The United States was the first to create scientific management, and its industry and commerce have taken off rapidly. Other countries have adopted it and achieved remarkable results. Why should our country lag behind for so long? The Ministry of Industry and Commerce has already established a Scientific Management Research Association to promote it. It is hoped that all companies above the medium level in the country will rise up and adopt it. There are a large number of small and medium-sized businesses and factories, and they are like a sheet of loose sand, without any organization. The government has never asked about them. How can they do rationalization? I believe that as long as the personnel in charge of these businesses are careful to study things and use common sense, they will be able to eliminate a lot of consumption, and there will be many improvements. Regarding scientific issues, the first thing they need to do is to organize themselves. The second thing is for the government to do its best to guide and assist them. Now I will give a real example to illustrate this. There are more than 1.3 million independent craftsmen in Germany, employing more than 4 million apprentices and artisans. They have organized the Craftsmen's Association and divided it into 62 branches according to region. Within a region, they are further divided into small industry associations according to occupation, which recruit apprentices, hold examinations, elect officers, pay pensions, and handle registration. However, the government must send personnel to supervise the examinations and elections. In 1924, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce established a Craftsmen's Committee to resolve disputes in legal matters, provide loans when necessary in economic matters, and have experts study the improvement of various handicrafts and matters such as hygiene and safety in knowledge matters, and disseminate the results to the craftsmen concerned, either in writing or through lectures, and sometimes even show movies or slides. If this is done, with the people and the government working together, what can't be done? What is so difficult about rationalization? The rationalization of the above-mentioned small factories can all be applied to large factories and increase its importance. The matters that should be paid attention to in large factories are further described separately below. Labor-capital relations, is a very big problem in large factories. In our country, it has gradually become tense. Employers and managers lack world vision and scientific knowledge. Once they encounter this difficulty, they are at a loss. As a result, various industries are stagnating. Various countries have also had such disputes, but since the adoption of rationalization or scientific management, they have gradually decreased. This is because the lives of workers should be stabilized, and the personality of workers should be taken care of. The reasons why workers are unwilling to work hard should be studied calmly and peacefully. If there are difficulties in their families, help them solve them. If there are unfavorable places in their working environment, try to improve them. Reward their savings, encourage them to invest, and increase their salaries according to statistics such as work performance, length of service, and number of children. In addition to shareholders and employees, workers can also receive a considerable portion of the profits. In short, make the labor and capital sides one, sharing benefits and sharing losses. Then, labor will naturally work hard, and all kinds of consumption can be saved. Regarding affairs, they must be handled strictly. Regarding regulations, they must be strictly implemented. All scientific methods must be adopted as much as possible to increase production. By doing this with one heart and one mind, the money saved and the increased income will definitely be enough to offset the expenses added to labor welfare and there will be a surplus. This is one of the reasons for the rapid development of industry in the United States. It is not to be ignored. (To be continued)
